            </source>
            Sorry, your browser either has JavaScript disabled or does not have any supported player.
            <br/>
            You can
            <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/43/Emotions_%28Mariah_Carey_song_-_sample%29.ogg">
             download the clip
            </a>
            or
            <a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Special:MyLanguage/Extension:TimedMediaHandler/Client_download">
             download a player
            </a>
            to play the clip in your browser.
           </audio>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">
          A sample from the song's final chorus, featuring Carey's usage of the whistle register.
         </div>
        </div>
        <hr/>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em">
        <span>
         <i>
          Problems playing this file? See
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           media help
          </a>
          .
         </i>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Three commercial singles were released from
      <i>
       Emotions
      </i>
      . The album's lead single of
      <a href="/wiki/Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Emotions (Mariah Carey song)">
       the same name
      </a>
      became Carey's fifth chart topper in the United States, making her the only act in history to have their first five singles reach the charts summit in the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lamb_18-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-lamb-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Hot_100_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Hot_100-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally, "
      <a href="/wiki/Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Emotions (Mariah Carey song)">
       Emotions
      </a>
      " topped the singles chart in Canada, reached the top five in New Zealand, and peaked within the top twenty in Australia, the Netherlands and the United Kingdom.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The song garnered positive critical response, with Bill Lamb from
      <a href="/wiki/About.com" title="About.com">
       About.com
      </a>
      rating it "among her best."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lamb_18-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-lamb-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Steve Morse from
      <i>
       The Boston Globe
      </i>
      called Carey's high registers in the song a "feeling of pure joy," whereas Jan DeKnock from the
      <i>
       Chicago Tribune
      </i>
      described Carey's voice as "breathtaking."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morse_20-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-morse-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deknock_21-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-deknock-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The song's music video features different scenes of Carey singing and enjoying herself throughout a car ride by the countryside, as well as a small celebration with several dancers.
     </p>
     <p>
      The album's second release, "
      <a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Let_Go_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Can't Let Go (Mariah Carey song)">
       Can't Let Go
      </a>
      ", only reached the number two position on the
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">
       Hot 100
      </a>
      , failing to top the chart due to
      <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">
       Columbia
      </a>
      's retraction of the single in order to boost sales of the album.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Hot_100_52-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Hot_100-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Aside from Canada, where it attained a peak of number three, "Can't Let Go" performed weakly across continental Europe, reaching the top twenty in only the UK.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The song's corresponding video was filmed in black and white, and featured Carey's hair in a straightened style for the first time in her career. The video predominantly features close-up scenes of Carey by a small outdoor fountain, as well as blooming white roses. "
      <a href="/wiki/Make_It_Happen_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Make It Happen (Mariah Carey song)">
       Make It Happen
      </a>
      " was released as the third and final single from
      <i>
       Emotions
      </i>
      on April 4, 1992. It peaked at number five in the United States, and as "Can't Let Go", charted weakly throughout Europe, coming in at number seven in Canada, seventeen in the UK, and thirty-five and forty-seven in Australia and the Netherlands, respectively.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Hot_100_52-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Hot_100-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The song was praised by critics; Morse called it "a clear slice of spiritual autobiography," and called the last chorus "glorious."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morse_20-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-morse-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Similarly, DeKnock called the song "upbeat and inspirational."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deknock_21-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-deknock-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The video filmed for "Make It Happen" featured Carey performing in front of an audience in a large cathedral-like church, alongside back-up singers and child dancers.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">
       Promotion
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Promotion">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      As with
      <i>
       Mariah Carey
      </i>
      the previous year, Carey did not embark on a tour to promote the album, due to the long travel times and strenuous schedules on her voice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro_64-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, while not touring the world, Carey promoted
      <i>
       Emotions
      </i>
      through an array of television and award show appearances, stateside and across Europe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro_64-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Carey performed "
      <a href="/wiki/Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Emotions (Mariah Carey song)">
       Emotions
      </a>
      " live for the first time at the 1991
      <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" title="MTV Video Music Award">
       MTV Video Music Awards
      </a>
      , backed by several male and female back up vocalists.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro_64-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following the award show appearance, she sang "Emotions" on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Arsenio_Hall_Show" title="The Arsenio Hall Show">
        The Arsenio Hall Show
       </a>
      </i>
      , airing on September 23, 1991. Additionally, Carey performed the song at the
      <a href="/wiki/1992_Soul_Train_Music_Awards" title="1992 Soul Train Music Awards">
       1992 Soul Train Music Awards
      </a>
      , and on British music program and talk show
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">
        Top of the Pops
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Des_O%27Connor" title="Des O'Connor">
        Des O'Connor
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro2_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro2-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additional European stops included
      <i>
       Sondagstoppet
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Kulan
      </i>
      in Sweden during mid-September 1991. All of the above mentioned performances included "
      <a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Let_Go_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Can't Let Go (Mariah Carey song)">
       Can't Let Go
      </a>
      " as a secondary performance in the night.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro2_65-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro2-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "Can't Let Go" was sung on additional programs such as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">
        Saturday Night Live
       </a>
      </i>
      , a pre-filmed studio clip on
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Today_(NBC_program)" title="Today (NBC program)">
        The Today Show
       </a>
      </i>
      . While the album's final single "
      <a href="/wiki/Make_It_Happen_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Make It Happen (Mariah Carey song)">
       Make It Happen
      </a>
      " was released only months after
      <i>
       Emotions
      </i>
      release, the song was not performed during the album's original chart run, however making its way onto the set-list of several of Carey following tours.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro2_65-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro2-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On February 26, 1992, Carey performed "
      <a href="/wiki/If_It%27s_Over" title="If It's Over">
       If It's Over
      </a>
      " at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/34th_Grammy_Awards" title="34th Grammy Awards">
       34th annual
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Award
      </a>
      , with a full orchestra and several back up singers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro_64-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_accolades">
       Awards and accolades
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Emotions_(Mariah_Carey_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Awards and accolades">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Throughout 1992, Carey, the album and its accompanying singles received recognition by the music industry in the form of several awards. At the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_1992" title="American Music Awards of 1992">
       19th annual
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award" title="American Music Award">
       American Music Awards
      </a>
      , Carey took home the award for
      <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award_for_Favorite_Soul/R%26B_Female_Artist" title="American Music Award for Favorite Soul/R&amp;B Female Artist">
       Favorite Soul/R&amp;B Female Artist
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro3_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro3-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At the 3rd annual
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award" title="Billboard Music Award">
       Billboard Music Awards
      </a>
      , Carey took home two trophies for the album and "Emotions", Top Female Album Artist and Top Female Single.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro3_66-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro3-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally, Carey was nominated for two
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Award
      </a>
      at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/34th_Grammy_Awards" title="34th Grammy Awards">
       34th annual ceremony
      </a>
      , for
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Producer_of_the_Year,_Non-Classical" title="Grammy Award for Producer of the Year, Non-Classical">
       Producer of the Year
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">
       Best Female Pop Vocal Performance
      </a>
      , losing in both categories.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro3_66-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-shapiro3-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      All three of the album's singles were awarded
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcast_Music_Incorporated" title="Broadcast Music Incorporated">
       BMI Pop Awards
      </a>
      in 1993.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
